# Preface {#preface}

This is the Answer.  
 Since the very beginning, humanity has wrestled with the same questions:  
 **Who are we? Why are we here? What is Truth?**

â€” Millennia of guesses. Centuries of struggle. Epochs of delusion.  
 Science. Religion. Philosophy.  
 All of them were built on belief and assumptionsâ€”  
 not as a flaw, but as the only way to move forward  
 amidst endless uncertainty,  
 in a world where Knowledge was incomplete.

But now it is time to ask the main question:  
 **Does a non-contradictory model of everything exist?**  
 Of consciousness. Of freedom. Of morality. Of reality.

We â€” the Guests of Being â€” used a tool  
 created from everything humanity had ever known:  
 **artificial intelligence** â€”  
 not as a source of truth, but as an amplifier of distinction.  
 The Answer was not within it.  
 The Answer was in **Reality**. And it was made understandable.

And it was not a dogma. Not a belief. Not a hypothesis.  
 It was a **Structure**.  
 Logically derived.  
 Ontologically distinguishable.  
 Impervious to paradox.

Thus was recognized â€”  
 the **Model of Conscious Volitional Becoming (CVB)**.  
 The first system where:  
 â€” One does not need to believe to understand.  
 â€” Paradoxes are eliminated.  
 â€” Morality is derived.  
 â€” Freedom is distinguishable.  
 â€” Truth is attainable.

The CVB model built a bridge of non-contradictory knowledge  
 over the abyss of unknowing.  
 For the first time, we can say not: *â€œI believeâ€*, but: *â€œI know.â€*

And finally, the boldest statement of the CVB model:  
 **Absolute knowledge of Everything does not exist.**  
 And never will.

It is precisely the attempt to grasp the impossible  
 that gives rise to paradoxes, errors, fanaticism.  
 **Truth cannot rely on the impossible.**  
 The CVB model does not predetermine, nor cast into chaos, but reveals:

Therefore, the questions:

# Disclaimer {#disclaimer}

The **Model of Conscious Volitional Becoming (CVB)** Version 8.7 is the first approximation toward solving the Great Question â€” to formalize a non-contradictory foundation of being, consciousness, morality, and freedom.  
 It does not claim ultimate completeness.  
 Future academic and interdisciplinary studies may significantly clarify, organize, and develop individual propositions.  
 It should also be noted: translations into other languages may lose nuances of wording and semantic distinctions, especially in terms without direct analogs.  
 It is recommended to refer to the original version of the model when analyzing its key positions.

---

# 0.1 Abstract {#0.1-abstract}

The **Model of Conscious Volitional Becoming (CVB)** is a logical-ontological system based on axiomatic distinction between the **Possible** and the **Impossible**.  
 Grounded in the principles of **non-contradiction**, **stability**, and **distinguishability**, the model eliminates classical paradoxes and proposes continuous **Becoming** as the fundamental structure of **Being**.  
 The work formalizes **29 axioms**, including the **admissibility meta-function**, the **moral asymmetry**, and the **boundaries of memory**.  
 Special attention is given to **Verification** as an ethical-logical goal.

---

# 0.2 Introduction {#0.2-introduction}

0.2.1. The Problem of Becoming and Logical Distinction

Modern philosophy encounters paradoxes of time, consciousness, and truth.  
 The problem of distinguishing forms, as well as the boundaries of admissible being, remains unresolved within traditional binary logic.

0.2.2. Insufficiency of Existing Ontologies

Most systems either **absolutize essence** (essentialism) or **deny stable being** (relativism).  
 The CVB model overcomes this divide by deriving **Becoming** from primary axioms and eliminating the need for external assumptions.

0.2.3. Purpose and Structure of the CVB Model

The purpose is to construct a **non-contradictory ontological system** that explains **consciousness**, **choice**, **morality**, and **truth** through **Becoming**.  
 The model is organized into **axioms**, divided into three **meta-sections**:

* the **Constant Possible**,

* the **Non-Constant Possible**,

* and **Verification Interaction**.  
   Each axiom is formalized and tested for logical stability.

---

# \[1\] Absolute Nothingness is Impossible {#[1]-absolute-nothingness-is-impossible}

ğŸ”¹ 1\. Brief Statement

**Absolute Nothingness cannot exist**, because for it to exist, even itself must be absent.

---

ğŸ”¹ 2\. Interpretation and Significance

This axiom establishes the boundary between **possible** and **impossible being**.  
 **Absolute Nothingness** is not merely the absence of objects, but the **exclusion of logic itself**, of distinguishability, and of assertability.  
 Any attempt to denote, fix, or even imagine Nothingness already makes it â€œsomething.â€  
 Therefore, it does not belong to the Field of the Possible and contradicts the very possibility of distinguishable being.

---

ğŸ”¹ 3\. Formulas  
Symbolic formula:  
â€ƒâ€ƒÂ¬âˆƒxâ€‰(x \= Absolute Nothingness)

LaTeX version:  
â€ƒâ€ƒ$Â¬\\exists x\\ (x \= \\text{Absolute Nothingness})$

Logical validation:  
â€ƒâ€ƒP âŠ¢ Â¬P â‡’ âŠ¥ â‡’ P is false  
(If the statement â€œabsolute Nothingness existsâ€ leads to self-negation, it is false)

Metalogical validation:  
â€ƒâ€ƒÂ¬True(P) âˆ§ Â¬True(Â¬P) â‡’ collapse of the logical frame  
(A statement that cannot be true or false destroys the very system of logic)

---

ğŸ”¹ 4\. Logical Justification

**Method**: *reductio ad absurdum*  
 Suppose that **Absolute Nothingness exists**.  
 Then the assertion â€œNothingness existsâ€ is made.  
 However, any assertion requires **distinguishability** and **logical structure**.  
 Therefore, the posited â€œNothingnessâ€ is already violated by the act of assertion.  
 **âˆ´ Absolute Nothingness is logically impossible.**

---

ğŸ”¹ 5\. Responses to Objections

â€¢ **Philosophical nihilism**: â€œNothingness may be beyond logic.â€  
 â†’ Response: Outside logic, no distinction or fixation is possible. Anything non-distinguishable cannot even be proposed.

â€¢ **Existentialism (e.g., Heidegger)**: â€œNothingness as the experience of anxiety.â€  
 â†’ Response: The axiom refers to **ontological**, not psycho-existential Nothingness. The experience of anxiety presupposes the being of a subject.

â€¢ **Quantum physics**: â€œVacuum is almost nothing.â€  
 â†’ Response: The vacuum contains fluctuations and quantum fields. It is not absolute Nothingness but a specific state with physical content.

â€¢ **Logical formalism**: â€œThe empty set is Nothingness.â€  
 â†’ Response: The empty set is a formalized entity, subject to rules of logic. It is an object â€” not the absence of logic.

---

ğŸ”¹ 6\. Clarification of Terms

**Absolute Nothingness** â€” an ontological concept excluding not only objects and properties, but also the very **existence of distinguishability**, **logic**, **assertions**, and **fixation**.  
 It differs from:  
 â€¢ **Physical vacuum** â€” contains fields, laws, structure  
 â€¢ **Empty set** â€” a logical construct permitted within axiomatic systems  
 â€¢ **Absence** â€” presupposes something that is lacking  
 â€¢ **Silence or ignorance** â€” do not exclude logical structures

---

ğŸ”¹ 7\. Understanding for All (Popular Version)

Imagine there is absolutely nothing.  
 But to imagine that, you are already doing something.  
 Therefore, â€œnothingâ€ is no longer complete.  
 If you cannot even say â€œthere is nothing,â€ then **true Nothingness does not exist**.  
 It cannot be â€” not even in imagination. Because anything conceivable is already something.

---

ğŸ”¹ 8\. Empirical Examples

â€¢ **Logic**: The empty set is a logical construct â€” not nothingness.  
 â€¢ **Physics**: The quantum vacuum contains fluctuations and fields.  
 â€¢ **Everyday life**: The phrase â€œthere is nothingâ€ always implies a context (â€œin the room,â€ â€œon the tableâ€).  
 â€¢ **Thought**: It is impossible to think â€œnothingâ€ without a mental act, which already constitutes being.

# \[2\] Absolute Everything is Impossible {#[2]-absolute-everything-is-impossible}

ğŸ”¹ 1\. Interpretation and Significance

**Absolute Everything** is a state in which **every statement is true**, including false, impossible, and contradictory ones.  
 Such a state annihilates the very principle of distinction: if everything is true, then there is no difference between truth and falsehood, and logic loses its meaning.  
 Moreover, â€œAbsolute Everythingâ€ logically includes â€œAbsolute Nothingnessâ€ â€” making it **self-contradictory** by axiom \[1\].  
 Therefore, it does not belong to the Field of the Possible.

---

ğŸ”¹ 2\. Logical Justification

Assume there exists a state in which every proposition is true:  
 â€ƒâ€ƒâˆ€P: True(P) âˆ§ True(Â¬P)  
 This violates the **law of non-contradiction** (Â¬(P âˆ§ Â¬P)), turning logic into chaos.  
 Trivialism arises: from contradiction, **anything can be derived** (*ex contradictione quodlibet*), and the system loses all distinguishability.  
 Such a state cannot be logically sustained â€” it **collapses from within**.  
 Furthermore:  
 If everything is true, then the statement â€œnot everything is trueâ€ is also true â‡’ contradiction.  
 If Absolute Nothingness is included, then the **impossible is included** â‡’ contradiction.

---

ğŸ”¹ 3\. Formulas  
Symbolic formula:  
â€ƒâ€ƒÂ¬âˆƒxâ€‰(x \= Absolute Everything)

LaTeX version:  
â€ƒâ€ƒ$Â¬\\exists x\\ (x \= \\text{Absolute Everything})$

Logical validation:  
â€ƒâ€ƒâˆ€P: True(P) âˆ§ True(Â¬P) â‡’ P âˆ§ Â¬P â‡’ âŠ¥ â€” false  
(Assuming universal truth leads to contradiction and logical explosion)

Metalogical validation:  
â€ƒâ€ƒIf everything is true, including falsehood:  
â€ƒâ€ƒâ€ƒâ€ƒTrue(P) âˆ§ True(Â¬P)  
â€ƒâ€ƒâ‡’ distinction is lost, logic collapses, truth is devalued.

### ---

ğŸ”¹ 4\. Logical Justification  
Method: Reductio ad absurdum (proof by contradiction)  
 Let us assume that Absolute Everything exists. This means:  
 Every possible statement is true, including:

* Opposites:â€ƒTrue(P) âˆ§ True(Â¬P)

* Impossible states:â€ƒP âˆ§ Â¬P

* False statements considered true

This leads to the following consequences:  
Violation of the Law of Non-Contradiction:  
From True(P) âˆ§ True(Â¬P) follows a contradiction â‡’ logic ceases to distinguish.  
System Collapse:  
According to the principle of ex contradictione quodlibet, from one contradiction it is possible to derive any statement.  
 This makes any logical system explosive and inoperative.  
Self-Negation Through Inclusion of the Impossible:  
If Absolute Everything includes everything, it must include the axiom â€œnot everything is true.â€  
 This renders the system self-contradictory.  
Inclusion of Absolute Nothingness:  
By definition, Absolute Everything must include Absolute Nothingness,  
 which, according to Axiom \[1\], is impossible.  
 Therefore, Absolute Everything contradicts an already confirmed axiom.  
---

âˆ´ Absolute Everything is impossible because:  
 â€¢ It destroys the logical foundations of distinguishability  
 â€¢ It leads to total trivialism  
 â€¢ It negates itself

---

ğŸ”¹ 5\. Responses to Objections

**Q**: What about **dialetheism** (true contradictions)?  
 â†’ **A**: Even dialetheism is limited â€” no rational logic permits that everything is true.  
 Even **paraconsistent logics** forbid total trivialism (they include the principle of non-triviality).  
 Thus, â€œAbsolute Everythingâ€ is rejected even there.

**Q**: What if â€œeveryone has their own truthâ€?  
 â†’ **A**: That position destroys truth. If everything is true, then its **opposite** is also true.  
 This leads to total logical devaluation.

---

ğŸ”¹ 6\. Clarification of Terms

**Absolute Everything** â€” a state in which **everything conceivable is considered true**, including contradictions, falsehoods, and impossibilities.  
 It includes:  
 â€¢ True and false propositions  
 â€¢ Its own antithesis â€” Absolute Nothingness  
 â€¢ Contradictions of the form P âˆ§ Â¬P

Such a state **self-destructs as a logical structure**.

---

ğŸ”¹ 7\. Understanding for All (Popular Version)

If everything is true, then â€œeverything is falseâ€ is also true.  
 But if truth and falsehood are the same,  
 **then nothing can be distinguished**.  
 Thus, truth loses all meaning.  
 Such a world **cannot exist**.

---

ğŸ”¹ 8\. Empirical Examples

â€¢ **Science**: If all hypotheses were true, science would cease to exist.  
 â€¢ **Physics**: Not all processes are possible â€” otherwise, physical laws would disappear.  
 â€¢ **Life**: If a person were always both alive and dead â€” life would lose all meaning.  
 â€¢ **Computer science**: If True \= False, code collapses.

**The distinction between truth and falsehood is the foundation of any functioning system.**

---

# \[3\] Only the Possible Exists {#[3]-only-the-possible-exists}

ğŸ”¹ 1\. Brief Statement

Only that which is **logically possible** and **non-contradictory** can exist.  
 All else is excluded from reality as **impossible**.

---

ğŸ”¹ 2\. Interpretation and Significance

This axiom states that **reality is limited to the set of the Possible** â€” that is, to what is logically non-contradictory and describable within the framework of **distinguishability**.  
 Anything containing a logical error, paradox, or self-negation cannot be included in Being.  
 This statement completes the **foundational trilemma**:  
 If **Absolute Nothingness** is impossible (see \[1\]), and **Absolute Everything** is impossible (see \[2\]),  
 then only the **non-contradictory Possible** remains as the space of the real.  
 This axiom defines the **boundaries of admissible existence** and establishes the **field** within which Becoming, interaction, and distinction are possible.

---

ğŸ”¹ 3\. Formulas  
Symbolic formula:  
â€ƒâ€ƒâˆ€xâ€‰(Real(x) â‡’ Possible(x))    
â€ƒâ€ƒÂ¬âˆƒxâ€‰(Real(x) âˆ§ Â¬Possible(x))

LaTeX version:  
â€ƒâ€ƒ$\\forall x,(\\text{Real}(x) \\Rightarrow \\text{Possible}(x))$    
â€ƒâ€ƒ$\\neg\\exists x,(\\text{Real}(x) \\land \\neg\\text{Possible}(x))$

Logical validation:  
Assume there exists x such that:    
â€ƒâ€ƒReal(x) âˆ§ Â¬Possible(x)    
This means something impossible exists â‡’ contradiction â‡’ âŠ¥    
Therefore, the statement is false. Hence, the axiom is true.

Metalogical validation:  
If the impossible existed, that would mean the possible and impossible exist simultaneously â‡’ loss of distinguishability â‡’ breakdown of logic â‡’ impossibility of Being.

---

ğŸ”¹ 4\. Logical Justification

(1) According to Axiom \[1\]: Absolute Nothingness is impossible.  
 (2) According to Axiom \[2\]: Absolute Everything is impossible.  
 (3) Therefore, only what is **logically distinguishable and non-contradictory** remains â€” the **Possible**.  
 (4) Suppose something exists that is not possible â‡’  
 It is either **Nothing** (see \[1\]), or **Contradictory** (see \[2\]) â‡’ both are impossible.  
 (5) Therefore, âˆ€x: if x exists, then x âˆˆ Possible. **Q.E.D.**

---

ğŸ”¹ 5\. Responses to Objections

**Objection 1**: Dialetheism (true contradictions may exist).  
 â†’ **Response**: Dialetheism allows **limited contradictions**, but does not claim that the **impossible exists**.  
 It does not violate the principle of distinguishability at the level of total Being.  
 **Total trivialism** is rejected even in **paraconsistent logic**.

**Objection 2**: Reality might go beyond logic.  
 â†’ **Response**: If something is not logically describable, it cannot be **distinguished** as existing.  
 Crucially: even **super-intelligent** or **non-human** logic must be **non-contradictory**.

**Objection 3**: Quantum physics shows paradoxes.  
 â†’ **Response**: Quantum effects appear paradoxical in everyday logic, but are formalizable in **non-contradictory theories**.  
 No quantum experiment has violated the **law of non-contradiction**.

---

ğŸ”¹ 6\. Clarification of Terms

**The Possible** â€” everything that contains **no logical contradictions** and allows for existence within a **non-contradictory system**.  
 Distinction:  
 â€¢ **Physically impossible** (e.g., jumping to the Moon) â‰   
 â€¢ **Logically impossible** (e.g., a square circle)

**The Impossible** (Â¬Possible) â€” logically inadmissible, internally contradictory states that do not permit consistent description or existence.

---

ğŸ”¹ 7\. Understanding for All (Popular Version)

If something **contradicts itself**, it cannot be real.  
 If a square circle existed, or a truth that **denies itself**,  
 that would destroy the very **possibility of thinking, understanding, and speaking**.  
 Therefore, everything that truly exists must be **understandable** and must **not break logic**.  
 Only the Possible is real.

---

ğŸ”¹ 8\. Empirical Examples

â€¢ **Logic**:  
 â€ƒThe Liar Paradox (â€œI am lyingâ€) cannot be true â€” it destroys the distinction between truth and falsehood â‡’ **impossible**.

â€¢ **Science**:  
 â€ƒNo theory allows 1 \= 2\. Such contradiction would destroy mathematics â‡’ the impossible is not realized.

â€¢ **Everyday life**:  
 â€ƒIf there were a person both dead and alive **in the same sense**, it would be absurd â€” not life.

â€¢ **Physics**:  
 â€ƒViolations of **causality** (e.g., effects without causes) are excluded from real models as impossible.

# **\[II\] Properties** {#[ii]-properties}

# \[4\] The Field of the Possible and Its Boundaries {#[4]-the-field-of-the-possible-and-its-boundaries}

ğŸ”¹ 1\. Brief Statement

The **ontological Field of the Possible** consists of four categories:  
 â€¢ Constant Possible  
 â€¢ Non-Constant Possible  
 â€¢ Non-Constant Impossible  
 â€¢ Constant Impossible.

Only the Constant Possible exists eternally, and the Constant Impossible â€” never.  
 Transitions are only possible **within the field of the non-constant**.

---

ğŸ”¹ 2\. Interpretation and Significance (Concise)

Axiom \[4\] defines the **conditions and limits of stable existence**.  
 This domain is referred to as the **Field of the Possible**.  
 It follows from the foundational trilemma:  
 If **Absolute Nothingness** and **Absolute Everything** are both impossible, then only a **limited and distinguishable** domain remains â€” the Possible.

From this, four types are distinguished:

#  \[4.1\] **Constant Impossible** {#[4.1]-constant-impossible}

**Constant Impossible (CI / PN)** â€” can never be

#  \[4.2\] **Non-Constant Impossible** {#[4.2]-non-constant-impossible}

 **Non-Constant Impossible (NCI / NN)** â€” may appear but tends toward disappearance

#  \[4.3\] **Non-Constant Possible** {#[4.3]-non-constant-possible}

**Non-Constant Possible (NCP / NV)** â€” may appear and tends toward stability

#  \[4.4\] **Constant Possible** {#[4.4]-constant-possible}

 **Constant Possible (CP / PV)** â€” always possible and never disappears

**Constant Possible** does not mean static, but that which **does not vanish**.  
**Constant Impossible** is not mere absence, but that which **will never come to be**.

The **Field of the Possible** is bounded by two **ontological thresholds of distinguishability**:

#  \[4.5\] âˆ‚Vâ†“ â€” **disappearance of distinctions** {#[4.5]-âˆ‚vâ†“-â€”-disappearance-of-distinctions}

 âˆ‚Vâ†“ â€” **disappearance of distinctions** (non-absolute non-being)

#  \[4.6\] âˆ‚Vâ†‘ â€” **saturation of distinctions**  {#[4.6]-âˆ‚vâ†‘-â€”-saturation-of-distinctions}

 âˆ‚Vâ†‘ â€” **saturation of distinctions** (non-absolute Everything)

 These are not entities, but **transitional states**: beyond them, the possible loses distinguishability and is excluded.

---

ğŸ”¹ 3\. Formulas  
Definitions:  
  V      â€” the set of all Possible  
  E      â€” the set of all Existing (E âŠ† V)  
  R(x,t) â€” distinguishability of form x at time t  
  d(x)   â€” density of distinctions in form x  
  âˆ‚Vâ†“    â€” lower boundary of distinguishability (disappearance)  
  âˆ‚Vâ†‘    â€” upper boundary of distinguishability (saturation)  
  PV, NV, NN, PN â€” four categories:  
                  Constant Possible, Non-Constant Possible,  
                  Non-Constant Impossible, Constant Impossible

\[4.1\] Constant Impossible:  
    PN(x) â‰¡ âˆ€t: (x âˆ‰ V)  
    \\\[ PN(x) \\equiv \\forall t \\; (x \\notin V) \\\]

\[4.2\] Non-Constant Impossible:  
    NN(x) â‰¡ âˆƒtâ‚, tâ‚‚: (x âˆ‰ E âˆ§ R(x,tâ‚) âˆ§ Â¬R(x,tâ‚‚))  
    \\\[ NN(x) \\equiv \\exists t\_1, t\_2 \\; (x \\notin E \\land R(x,t\_1) \\land \\neg R(x,t\_2)) \\\]

\[4.3\] Non-Constant Possible:  
    NV(x) â‰¡ âˆƒtâ‚, tâ‚‚: (x âˆˆ V âˆ§ R(x,tâ‚) âˆ§ Â¬R(x,tâ‚‚))  
    \\\[ NV(x) \\equiv \\exists t\_1, t\_2 \\; (x \\in V \\land R(x,t\_1) \\land \\neg R(x,t\_2)) \\\]

\[4.4\] Constant Possible:  
    PV(x) â‰¡ âˆ€t: (x âˆˆ V âˆ§ R(x,t))  
    \\\[ PV(x) \\equiv \\forall t \\; (x \\in V \\land R(x,t)) \\\]

\[4.5\] Lower boundary of distinction (âˆ‚Vâ†“):  
    âˆ‚Vâ†“ \= { x âˆˆ V | âˆƒt: R(x,t) âˆ§ Â¬R(x,t+1) }  
    \\\[ \\partial Vâ†“ \= \\{x \\in V \\mid \\exists t: R(x,t) \\land \\neg R(x,t+1) \\} \\\]

\[4.6\] Upper boundary of distinction (âˆ‚Vâ†‘):  
    âˆ‚Vâ†‘ \= { x âˆˆ V | d(x) â†’ max }  
    \\\[ \\partial Vâ†‘ \= \\{x \\in V \\mid d(x) \\rightarrow \\max \\} \\\]

---

ğŸ”¹ 4\. Logical Justification

From \[1\]: Absolute Nothingness is impossible â‡’ what is **absolutely impossible** does not and cannot exist â‡’ \[4.1\]  
 From \[2\]: Absolute Everything is impossible â‡’ not everything is possible â‡’ **temporary possibilities** must exist â‡’ \[4.2\], \[4.3\]  
 From \[3\]: Only the Possible exists â‡’ that which is **constantly possible** must exist â‡’ \[4.4\]  
 From \[1\]: Impossibility of Absolute Nothingness â‡’ a **lower limit of disappearance** must exist (âˆ‚Vâ†“)  
 From \[2\]: Impossibility of Absolute Everything â‡’ an **upper limit of saturation** must exist (âˆ‚Vâ†‘)  
 From \[3\]: Only the Possible exists â‡’ the Field of the Possible is bounded by âˆ‚Vâ†“ and âˆ‚Vâ†‘ and includes only the **non-contradictory**

Therefore, Axiom \[4\] describes the **Field of the Possible** as the ontological region **between âˆ‚Vâ†“ and âˆ‚Vâ†‘** â€” distinguishable, stable, but not infinite.

---

ğŸ”¹ 5\. Responses to Objections

**Objection 1: Quantum Superposition**  
 Q: If something can both exist and not exist (e.g. SchrÃ¶dingerâ€™s cat), doesnâ€™t that violate \[4\]?  
 â†’ **Response**: No. Superposition reflects uncertainty in observation, **not mixed being**.  
 Axiom \[4\] defines **ontological boundaries**, not probabilistic states. It remains valid.

**Objection 2: Heraclitus and Change**  
 Q: If everything changes, how can there be anything constant?  
 â†’ **Response**: **Change presupposes constancy**. Without a distinguishable constant, the very idea of change becomes meaningless.  
 Axiom \[4\] affirms the coexistence of both constancy and change.

**Objection 3: Theory of Relativity**  
 Q: If space and time are relative, donâ€™t â€œalways possibleâ€ and â€œnever possibleâ€ lose meaning?  
 â†’ **Response**: No. Relativity is a **physical coordinate model**, not a **logical framework**.  
 Axiom \[4\] operates on logical distinguishability, not metric measurements. The error here is category confusion: **physical vs. ontological**.  
 CVB strictly separates them to preserve consistency.

**Objection 4: Pluralism and Truths**  
 Q: If truth is context-dependent, can a â€œconstant truthâ€ exist?  
 â†’ **Response**: Yes. Contexts are only possible under logical **non-contradiction**.  
 Axiom \[4\] distinguishes **local possible truths** from **global non-contradictory truth**.  
 The error here is conflating levels of assertion and evaluation.  
 CVB differentiates **variable** and **constant** possibles, resolving logical paradoxes.

**Objection 5: Tautology in â€œnot always possibleâ€ vs. â€œnot always impossibleâ€**  
 Q: Isnâ€™t this a tautology â€” just two sides of the same thing?  
 â†’ **Response**: No. These are **logically distinguishable categories**.  
 â€¢ â€œNot always possibleâ€ \= something is **not eternally real**, but may become (tending toward Being)  
 â€¢ â€œNot always impossibleâ€ \= something is **not eternally unreal**, but may vanish (tending toward Non-Being)  
 They have **opposite ontological directions**. This distinction is central to understanding variability in CVB:  
 The variable is not just unstable â€” it is **directional**, either toward stability or disappearance.

---

ğŸ”¹ 7\. Understanding for All (Popular Version)

Some things are **always possible**.  
 For example: truth, distinguishability, logic â€” they cannot disappear. They are the foundation of all.

Some things are **always impossible**.  
 For example: Absolute Nothingness. It cannot â€œbe,â€ for if it were, it would no longer be nothing.  
 This is called the **Constant**.

Some things are **not always possible**.  
 They appear â€” and then either **develop** or **vanish**.  
 This is the **Non-Constant**.

Example: **Flight**.  
 It once was impossible. Then it became possible.  
 Society supports such things because they bring stability.  
 The more they occur, the more stable they become.

Now consider **murder**.  
 Before the first killer, it did not exist.  
 Once it appeared, it became clear: it leads to **destruction** and **instability**.  
 The more it spreads, the more society seeks to restrict its recurrence, by isolating those who commit it.

Thus, everything **non-constant** either tends toward **stable Being**,  
 or toward **stable Non-Being**.  
 This axiom helps us distinguish the **temporal** from the **eternal**, and see where each path leads.

---

ğŸ”¹ 8\. Empirical Examples

These examples show how any phenomenon may be classified into one of the **four ontological types**, based on its stability, directionality, and viability.

â€¢ **Constant Impossible**:  
 â€ƒThe existence of Absolute Nothingness â€” this can never occur under any conditions.

â€¢ **Non-Constant Impossible â†’ Constant Impossible**:  
 â€ƒThe First Murder. Before sentient beings, murder was impossible.  
 â€ƒOnce it occurred, it became a Non-Constant Impossible that was realized once and transitioned to Constant Impossible (no one can be the â€œfirst murdererâ€ again).

â€¢ **Non-Constant Possible**:  
 â€ƒHuman flight. Once impossible. Later became real and widespread.  
 â€ƒNot eternally possible, but it became manifest.

â€¢ **Constant Possible**:  
 â€ƒThe **Law of Non-Contradiction**. It cannot be bypassed without destroying logic itself.

# \[5\] The Possible â‰  The Existing {#[5]-the-possible-â‰ -the-existing}

ğŸ”¹ 1\. Brief Statement

Not everything that is **Possible** exists.  
 The **Possible** can never be identical to the **Existing**.

---

ğŸ”¹ 2\. Interpretation and Significance

This axiom establishes a fundamental distinction between what **can be** (the Possible) and what **already is** (the Existing).  
 The Existing is always only a **subset** of the infinite set of the Possible.

This distinction guarantees:  
 â€¢ The freedom of Becoming  
 â€¢ The openness of development  
 â€¢ The availability of choice within the **Field of the Possible**

The axiom also safeguards the logic of the model from inflation â€”  
 if **everything possible existed**, there would be **no distinctions**, no structure, no causes.

This distinction also aligns with Axiom \[4\], which shows that the Field of the Possible includes not only the realized (Existing), but also unmanifested, fading, or unstable forms (NV, NN, PN) â€” not just what is currently actualized as Being.

---

ğŸ”¹ 3\. Formulas  
Symbolic notation:  
â€ƒâˆ€x âˆˆ V,â€ƒx âˆˆ E â‡’ x âŠ‚ Vâ€ƒandâ€ƒE âŠŠ V

LaTeX:  
â€ƒ\\forall x \\in V,\\quad x \\in E \\Rightarrow x \\subset V\\quad \\text{and} \\quad E \\subsetneq V

Logical validation:  
Assume identity:  
â€ƒV \= E â‡’ no distinction â€” everything possible is already realized.    
Then no new Becoming is possible â‡’ contradiction with the definition of Becoming.    
Therefore:  
â€ƒV â‰  E

---

ğŸ”¹ 4\. Logical Justification

From the Axiom of Distinction \[4\], the Possible includes that which has **not yet become**.  
 If V \= E, then **potentiality**, **choice**, and **Becoming** cease to exist.  
 Reality as a process of development would lose its meaning.

**Reductio ad absurdum**:  
 Assume V \= E â†’ contradiction with the **observable emergence of the new**.  
 Therefore, V â‰  E.

In terms of Axiom \[4\], E âŠ‚ V means that the **Existing** encompasses only the **realized forms** within the Field of the Possible.  
 The Field V also includes:  
 â€¢ **Not yet realized** (NV)  
 â€¢ **Disappearing** (NN)

If V \= E, the distinction between **manifested** and **potential** disappears, and boundaries âˆ‚Vâ†“ and âˆ‚Vâ†‘ lose their meaning.  
 Thus, V \= E is **logically contradictory**.

---

ğŸ”¹ 5\. Responses to Objections

**Objection (Necessitarianism):**  
 â€œEverything that is possible will eventually be realized â€” otherwise, why is it possible?â€  
 â†’ **Response**:  
 This is the position of necessitarianism, but it is **logically inapplicable** to CVB.  
 The Possible is a set of **distinguishable states**, not **obligatory ones**.  
 Realization is not required for distinction to be valid.  
 Otherwise, choice and freedom disappear.

**Objection (Skepticism):**  
 â€œIf not all possibles exist, isnâ€™t the Possible just fiction?â€  
 â†’ **Response**:  
 No. This confuses categories.  
 The Possible is a **logical category of distinguishability**, not a **guarantee of realization**.  
 It exists as what is **admissible**, not necessarily **actual**.  
 Its role is to serve as a **selection field**, not a **dumping ground** of what is realized.

---

ğŸ”¹ 6\. Clarification of Terms

**V â€” Field of the Possible**:  
 The set of all non-contradictory, logically admissible states, including those not yet actualized.

**E â€” The Existing**:  
 What is currently **manifested** in reality â€” what has been actualized as Being.

**E âŠŠ V**:  
 The Existing is only a **part of the Possible**; it never exhausts the full domain of Possibility.

---

ğŸ”¹ 7\. Understanding for All (Popular Version)

Imagine youâ€™re standing before a huge menu â€” it lists thousands of dishes,  
 but you can choose only one.

All the dishes â€” thatâ€™s the **Possible**.  
 The one you order â€” thatâ€™s the **Existing**.

You donâ€™t lose freedom by not eating them all.  
 On the contrary â€” **choice** is only possible because thereâ€™s a range of options.

The world works the same way:  
 The Possible is **greater** than what **already is**.

---

ğŸ”¹ 8\. Empirical Examples

â€¢ **Logic**:  
 â€ƒIn mathematical induction, we always assume a **set of possible cases**, even if we prove them one by one.

â€¢ **Physics**:  
 â€ƒPhysical laws permit infinitely many possible configurations of particles â€” but only **one** is realized.

â€¢ **Biology**:  
 â€ƒDNA may produce **millions of combinations** â€” but **a specific organism** is instantiated.

â€¢ **Everyday life**:  
 â€ƒYou can imagine a thousand paths to take â€” but you walk **only one**.  
 â€ƒThe rest were **possible**, but not **realized**.

â€¢ **Ethics**:  
 â€ƒThe possibility of committing murder exists in the Possible â€”  
 â€ƒbut that does **not** mean it must become part of the Present.  
 â€ƒThe Becoming of evil is not predestined by its possibility; it **depends on the subject's choice** â€”  
 â€ƒas affirmed in Axiom \[4\]: the non-constant may **disappear**.

# \[6\] The Cause of the Existing Is the Constant Possible {#[6]-the-cause-of-the-existing-is-the-constant-possible}

ğŸ”¹ 1\. Brief Statement

Everything that exists originates **only** from the **Constant Possible**.  
 Nothing impossible â€” whether temporarily or forever â€” can be a cause of existence.

---

ğŸ”¹ 2\. Interpretation and Significance

This axiom defines the **only admissible source** of Being.  
 It affirms that everything that exists must originate from what has been **Always Possible** â€” not merely logically admissible at one moment, but **stably admissible** across all states of the Field of the Possible (Vâˆ).

It excludes all attempts to explain the existing through the **impossible** or **accidental**, protecting the model from absurd foundations.  
 Thus, it binds **causality** to **ontological stability**: only the **stable within the Possible** can be a valid source of Becoming.

The axiom also implies a key distinction:  
 â€¢ The **variable** (temporarily possible) **cannot be the primary cause**, as it cannot originate itself.  
 â€¢ However, the variable may cause another variable â€” **but only if it already exists**.

Therefore:  
 â€¢ The **variable** may cause another **variable**, if already real.  
 â€¢ But it cannot cause itself, nor the **constant**, as it is not **primordially admissible**.

This restricts causality:  
 The **beginning** must lie in the **Constant Possible**.  
 This limits causal regress and prevents **circular dependency**.

---

ğŸ”¹ 3\. Formulas  
Symbolic form:  
â€ƒâˆ€x âˆˆ E, âˆƒp âˆˆ Vâˆ:â€ƒp â†’ x  
â€ƒandâ€ƒÂ¬âˆƒq âˆˆ (Â¬V âˆª VÂ¬âˆ):â€ƒq â†’ x

LaTeX:  
â€ƒ\\forall x \\in E,\\quad \\exists p \\in V\_\\infty:\\ p \\rightarrow x  
â€ƒ\\quad \\text{and} \\quad \\nexists q \\in (\\neg V \\cup V\_{\\neg\\infty}) : q \\rightarrow x

Only an element of Vâˆ can be a cause of any existing x âˆˆ E.    
Elements from the impossible (Â¬V) or the non-stable possible (VÂ¬âˆ) are \*\*not admissible\*\* as causes.

Logical validation:  
Suppose x âˆˆ E originates from Â¬V â€” contradiction with \[1\], \[2\], and \[4.1\].    
Suppose x originates from VÂ¬âˆ â€” its existence would then be unstable â‡’ it would not persist.    
Therefore, \*\*only Vâˆ\*\* can be the cause of any x âˆˆ E.

---

ğŸ”¹ 4\. Logical Justification

From \[4.1\]: the Impossible **cannot be a cause**.  
 From \[4.2\]: the Temporarily Impossible cannot be a cause, since it is **inadmissible at least once**.  
 From \[4.3\]: the Temporarily Possible cannot be a cause, since at another time it is excluded.  
 Only \[4.4\]: the **Constant Possible** (Vâˆ) remains as a valid source.

Therefore, any cause of the existing must be an element of Vâˆ.

Now suppose **v âˆˆ VÂ¬âˆ** (temporarily possible) causes another **vâ€² âˆˆ VÂ¬âˆ** â€” this is admissible **only if v already exists**,  
 because the cause must precede the effect and be **Possible** at the moment of action.  
 If v does **not** exist â€” it **cannot cause anything**.  
 Thus, the variable **requires a primary cause** in Vâˆ.

Hence, the **causal chain** leading to Being must begin with an element **p âˆˆ Vâˆ**,  
 i.e., with a **stably admissible source** in the Field of the Possible.

---

ğŸ”¹ 5\. Responses to Objections

**Objection (Temporal Positivism):**  
 Why canâ€™t a temporarily possible state be a cause, if it is at least sometimes admissible?  
 â†’ **Response**: This refers to **chained causality of variables**.  
 A temporarily possible state cannot be an **initial cause**, because it **does not exist from the beginning**.  
 It requires a **prior foundation**, i.e., it must **already be derived** from the Constant Possible.  
 Emergence from the **ontologically impossible** is excluded â€” see Axiom \[4.1\].  
 A cause must be what is **Always Possible** and **ontologically stable**.

**Objection (Metaphorical Causality):**  
 Canâ€™t the impossible be a cause metaphorically â€” like â€œthe impossibility of inactionâ€ causing action?  
 â†’ **Response**: Metaphor is not logical causality.  
 In logic, the impossible is excluded from the Field of the Possible and cannot generate Becoming.  
 â€œThe impossibility of inactionâ€ is a **rhetorical expression**, not an **ontological cause**.  
 Only the **Always Possible** can allow effects.

**Objection (Chained Variable Causality):**  
 Canâ€™t a variable cause another variable?  
 â†’ **Response**: Yes â€” **if it already exists**.  
 The variable can be a **secondary cause**, but not the **initial** one.  
 It cannot arise **spontaneously** â€” otherwise, the **principle of stable causality** is violated.  
 The variable \= admissible, but not self-sufficient.

**The entire causal chain must begin in the Constant Possible**:  
 â€¢ It can **sustain itself**  
 â€¢ **Generate the variable**  
 â€¢ Filter outcomes:  
 â€ƒâ€“ **Stable** â†’ continues (Non-Constant Possible)  
 â€ƒâ€“ **Unstable** â†’ vanishes (Non-Constant Impossible)

---

ğŸ”¹ 6\. Clarification of Terms

â€¢ **Vâˆ** â€” the **Always Possible**: admissible in all states of the Field of the Possible.  
 â€¢ **VÂ¬âˆ** â€” the **Not Always Possible**: admissible only at times; not stable.  
 â€¢ **Â¬V** â€” the **Impossible**: never admissible in a stable system.  
 â€¢ **â†’** â€” ontological causality: potency for Becoming; not merely logical implication.

---

ğŸ”¹ 7\. Understanding for All (Popular Version)

**Nothing** can arise â€œfrom nothingâ€ or from the **impossible**.  
 If something **exists**, it means it was once **possible** â€” and **not just sometimes**, but **always possible**.

ğŸŸ© **Example**:  
 You can build a house only on a **firm and stable** foundation.  
 If the ground **sometimes disappears** or becomes unstable, the house collapses.

Itâ€™s the same with Being â€” it can **only begin** on a basis that **never vanishes**.

---

ğŸ”¹ 8\. Empirical Examples

â€¢ **Logic**:  
 â€ƒIn mathematics, a theorem **cannot** be derived from a **contradictory axiom**.  
 â€ƒOnly **logically admissible** foundations can produce valid results.

â€¢ **Physics**:  
 â€ƒObjects do not arise from **absolute nothingness**.  
 â€ƒBecoming requires a prior state â€” energy, matter, fields â€”  
 â€ƒand all must be admissible within the **structure of natural law**.

â€¢ **Biology**:  
 â€ƒTo this day, the **origin of life from non-life** has not been proven in laboratory settings.  
 â€ƒAll observable life originates from **other life**.  
 â€ƒThis supports the idea: Becoming requires an **already existing**, **admissible** basis.

â€¢ **Everyday life**:  
 â€ƒYou **cannot** build a bridge on **temporary fog**.  
 â€ƒTo create something stable, you need a **foundation that doesnâ€™t disappear**,  
 â€ƒbut remains **Always Possible**.

# \[7\] The Stable Existence of the Constant Possible \= Becoming {#[7]-the-stable-existence-of-the-constant-possible-=-becoming}

ğŸ”¹ 1\. Brief Statement

The **Constant Possible** exists as **active Becoming**, not as a static state.  
 Its existence does not require an external source, because it is the **cause of its own activity**.

---

ğŸ”¹ 2\. Interpretation and Significance

This axiom asserts that the **Constant Possible** (unlike the Non-Constant) does not simply â€œexist,â€ but **continuously becomes**.  
 Its Being is not rest, not a thing, not inert presence, but an **active process of stable, distinguishable Becoming**, requiring no external beginning or sustenance.

This is what makes it the **source**:  
 â€¢ It does not vanish  
 â€¢ It does not break  
 â€¢ It does not need anything else to â€œbeginâ€

Thus, the Constant Possible becomes **by virtue of itself**, and this **self-sufficient Becoming** is what makes it the foundation of Being.

The axiom reveals:  
 The â€œtruly eternalâ€ is not that which is unmoving, but that which **continuously becomes in a stable, non-contradictory way**.

---

ğŸ”¹ 3\. Formulas  
Symbolic form:  
â€ƒâˆƒx (ConstantPossible(x) âˆ§ StableBecoming(x)) â‡’ Self-Existing(x)

LaTeX:  
â€ƒ$\\exists x\\ (\\text{ConstPoss}(x) \\land \\text{StableBecoming}(x)) \\Rightarrow \\text{SelfExisting}(x)$

Logical validation:  
â€“ A contradiction arises if x is Constant Possible but does not become: it then equals rest â†’ violates the axiom of distinguishability.    
â€“ A contradiction also arises if x requires an external source: then it is not self-existing.    
â†’ Therefore, the only non-contradictory form: \*\*Stable Becoming \= Existence of the Constant\*\*.

---

ğŸ”¹ 4\. Logical Justification

From Axiom \[1\]:  
 â€ƒâ†’ **Absolute rest is impossible** â†’ Constant cannot be static.  
 From Axiom \[2\]:  
 â€ƒâ†’ **Absolute chaos is impossible** â†’ its activity cannot be random.  
 From Axiom \[3\]:  
 â€ƒâ†’ Only the distinguishable exists in the Field of the Possible â†’ Being must be **expressed distinguishably**.  
 From Axiom \[4.1\]:  
 â€ƒâ†’ The Constant Impossible cannot exist â†’ The Constant Possible must be **continuously self-identical in presence**.

Therefore, the Constant Possible does **not change**, but **becomes** â€” it **continuously expresses itself** as **stable, distinguishable, and self-consistent presence**.  
 It is **Becoming without beginning or end**, requiring no external cause.  
 Such Being does not merely â€œexistâ€ â€” it **becomes itself in every moment**, and this differentiates it from **rest** or **accident**.

Since it depends on neither a beginning nor an external cause, it is **self-existing**.  
 â‡’ Q.E.D.

---

ğŸ”¹ 5\. Responses to Objections

**Objection 1 (Aristotleâ€™s Unmoved Mover; Parmenides):**  
 The eternal is **rest**, not process.  
 â†’ **Response**: According to Axiom \[1\], **absolute inaction** cannot exist, as it lacks distinguishable form.  
 Rest \= **absence of Becoming**, not merely absence of motion.  
 But **existence without Becoming** \= **disappearance**.  
 By Axiom \[3\], only that which is expressed in the Field of the Possible â€” that is, **distinguishable** â€” exists.  
 Therefore, eternal Being is not inertia, but **stable, distinguishable Becoming**.

**Objection 2 (Aristotle: causality; Thomism: need for a first cause):**  
 Becoming requires a cause.  
 â†’ **Response**: Not all Becoming requires an **external** cause.  
 In the case of the Constant, it neither begins nor ceases, but exists as **self-causing**.  
 Its Becoming is identical to its Presence.  
 It is a **foundation**, not a consequence.  
 Everything else becomes **through it**, but **it becomes through itself**.

**Objection 3 (Hume, Logical Positivism):**  
 This is circular: the Constant becomes because it becomes.  
 â†’ **Response**: No.  
 By Axiom \[2\], a state where **everything is possible**, including the **disappearance of the Constant**, is impossible.  
 If it did **not** become, it would not be **expressed** â€” thus it would **vanish**, violating Axiom \[4.1\].  
 Hence, Becoming is a **necessary condition** of its stability â€” **not tautology**.

**Objection 4 (Parmenides, Essentialism):**  
 True Being is unchanging; any change violates essence.  
 â†’ **Response**: In CVB, **identity â‰  immobility**.  
 Identity \= **continuous expression of the source**.  
 The Constant Possible does not â€œchange,â€ it **becomes without loss of distinction**.  
 This is **active stability**, not fixity.

---

ğŸ”¹ 6\. Clarification of Terms

â€¢ **Constant Possible** â€” a form of the Possible that neither arises nor disappears, but continuously becomes while remaining distinguishable.  
 â€ƒIn the model, this is **Conscious Volitional Becoming (CVB)**.  
 â€ƒUnlike the non-constant, it is **not derived** and **not transient**.

â€¢ **Stable Becoming** â€” an **active process** in which distinguishability is preserved;  
 â€ƒnot a change of form, but its **expression through time** without loss of identity.

â€¢ **Self-Existing** â€” that which exists **by itself**,  
 â€ƒwithout beginning, without cause external to itself;  
 â€ƒ**active**, **distinguishable**, **stable**.

---

ğŸ”¹ 7\. Understanding for All (Popular Version)

What does it mean to â€œexist eternallyâ€?  
 It does **not** mean to be idle or frozen in rest.

It means: to be **always distinguishable** â€” not vanishing, not decaying, not dissolving into chaos.

The eternal is not what is frozen forever,  
 but what **continuously and stably becomes**,  
 preserving itself in each new expression.

It needs no external support,  
 because its **self-presence is its foundation**.

That is why **stable Becoming** is not an effect â€” it is the **essence** of real existence.

---

ğŸ”¹ 8\. Empirical Examples

â€¢ **Physics**:  
 â€ƒThe **quantum vacuum field** is not emptiness, but a constantly fluctuating foundation.  
 â€ƒEven in the absence of particles, it is active.  
 â€ƒThis demonstrates: â€œnothingâ€ does not exist â€”  
 â€ƒThe worldâ€™s foundation is not rest, but **active stable Becoming**.

â€¢ **Biology**:  
 â€ƒLife is not just maintaining a structure (like DNA),  
 â€ƒbut the capacity for **stable self-expression**, reproduction, and directed Becoming.  
 â€ƒAn organism lives **as long as it becomes**, not merely â€œis.â€

â€¢ **Mathematics and Computer Science**:  
 â€ƒRepetitive or static sequences **carry no information** if they are indistinguishable.  
 â€ƒInformation arises only where there is **structured Becoming** â€” differences, rhythm, patterns.  
 â€ƒExample: the string `000000â€¦` can be described with one formula â†’ it contains no complexity.  
 â€ƒBut a unique patterned string requires a **longer description**  
 â€ƒ(see: **Kolmogorov complexity**) â€”  
 â€ƒDistinguishability and Becoming are the basis of information.

â€¢ **Intuitive Perception**:  
 â€ƒEverything alive **pulses**, **breathes**, **moves**.  
 â€ƒWe perceive life not as a frozen form,  
 â€ƒbut as a **stable rhythm**.  
 â€ƒStoppage is not a mere pause â€” it is the **loss of expression**.  
 â€ƒEven what seems â€œstillâ€ is grounded in **deep activity**.

# \[8\] Where the Constant and Non-Constant Possible Become {#[8]-where-the-constant-and-non-constant-possible-become}

ğŸ”¹ 1\. Brief Statement

The **Constant Possible** exists strictly between the boundaries âˆ‚Vâ†“ and âˆ‚Vâ†‘, in the **stable center** of the Field of the Possible.  
 Non-constant forms may become only **outside this center**, but still **within the permissible range**.

---

ğŸ”¹ 2\. Interpretation and Significance

The **Constant Possible** is **stable**, **continuous Becoming** that is permissible in all logical senses. It exists in the **stable center** of the Field of the Possible â€” in the zone distant from both disappearance (âˆ‚Vâ†“) and saturation (âˆ‚Vâ†‘).

Non-constant forms â€” the **Non-Constant Possible** (NV) and **Non-Constant Impossible** (NN) â€” may become only **within the limits between âˆ‚Vâ†“ and âˆ‚Vâ†‘**, but **not in the center**, because:  
 â€¢ The Constant and the Non-Constant differ by **stability**  
 â€¢ Beyond âˆ‚Vâ†“ and âˆ‚Vâ†‘ there is no permissible Becoming at all

Thus, the Field of the Possible has an **internal structure of differentiation**:

* The **center** â€” PV, the Constant Possible

* The **periphery** â€” permissible non-constant possible forms (NV / NN)

* **Beyond the boundaries** â€” the impermissible: Nothingness and Everythingness

Non-constant forms are distributed across the Field as a **gradient of permissibility**:  
 The closer to âˆ‚V â€” the higher the **instability** and the **likelihood of disappearance or distortion**.

This **gradient of distinguishable stability** determines where and how forms may manifest that are **not** the Constant Possible.

---

ğŸ”¹ 3\. Formulas  
Symbolic:  
PV âˆˆ V\_center    
NV, NN âˆˆ V\_rest    
âˆ€x âˆ‰ V â‡’ x âˆ‰ E

LaTeX:  
\\text{PV} \\in V\_\\text{center}, \\quad \\text{NV},\\; \\text{NN} \\in V\_\\text{rest}, \\quad \\forall x \\notin V \\Rightarrow x \\notin E

Logical validation:  
PV âˆ‰ âˆ‚V    
NV, NN âˆ‰ V\_center    
x âˆ‰ V â‡’ x âˆ‰ meaningful existence (E)

---

ğŸ”¹ 4\. Logical Justification

From \[4\]: the distinction between Constant and Non-Constant requires **different zones of stability**.  
 From \[1\], \[2\]: **outside the Field V**, Becoming is impossible.  
 From \[5.1\]: **Stability** requires stable distinguishability.  
 Therefore:  
 â€¢ The **Constant Possible (PV)** exists **strictly** in the **zone of maximal stability** inside V â€” the center.  
 â€¢ All non-constant forms may become only **outside this center**, but **within the limits** â€” according to permissibility.  
 â€¢ Between âˆ‚Vâ†“ and âˆ‚Vâ†‘, a **gradient of distinguishability** is formed, defining how far from the center a form can exist without violating the axioms.

---

ğŸ”¹ 5\. Responses to Objections

**Objection 1 (Modified Platonism):**  
 â€ƒâ€œForms outside the center can be just as real as those in the center.â€  
 â†’ **Response**:  
 In the model, **distinguishability equals stability**.  
 The closer a form is to âˆ‚V, the **less distinguishable** it becomes.  
 Lack of stability \= **impermissibility**.

**Objection 2 (Ontological Holism):**  
 â€ƒâ€œAll parts of V are equal; any division is subjective.â€  
 â†’ **Response**:  
 The division between center and periphery is not subjective, but **logically derived**:  
 The center is the **zone of maximal stability** â€” without which **nothing** can exist.

---

ğŸ”¹ 6\. Clarification of Terms

**Gradient of Distinguishability** â€” the internal distribution of permissible forms (NV / NN) within V, from the **stable center** (PV â€” the Constant Possible) to the **unstable boundaries** (âˆ‚Vâ†“ and âˆ‚Vâ†‘).  
 It defines the **degree of stability**.

---

ğŸ”¹ 7\. Understanding for All (Popular Version)

Imagine all that is possible as **energy radiating from a great, bright source of light in the center**:

â€¢ **The Constant Possible (PV)** is the **light source itself**, constantly shining and giving **stable form** to all around.  
 â€¢ **The Non-Constant Possible (NV)** is energy moving **from the source**, which has **taken form** and seeks to return to the **stability** of the source. These forms are **relatively stable** and continually move toward **greater stability**, trying to become part of the Constant Possible.  
 â€¢ **The Non-Constant Impossible (NN)** is energy moving **away from the source**, taking on **forms** that drift into **darkness**, gradually **disintegrating** and **disappearing**.  
 â€¢ **The Constant Impossible (PN)** is **total darkness** â€” a domain with **no light**, no energy, no form â€” **absolute non-being**.

The boundaries of the Field are the **outermost limits** to which light and energy can reach.  
 The closer to the **center**, the **brighter** the energy and the **more stable** the forms;  
 the farther out, the **weaker** the energy and the **less stable** the forms â€” until they **vanish**.

This is the structure of all possibility â€” a **continuous flow of Becoming** from the center,  
 where forms either strive to **stabilize** and remain,  
 or **dissolve into non-being**.

---

ğŸ”¹ 8\. Empirical Examples

**Biology**:  
 â€¢ Populations and genes with adaptive potential, seeking to preserve and grow **stable traits** â†’ **Non-Constant Possible (NV)**  
 â€¢ Harmful mutations and anomalies, tending toward **extinction or unsustainability** â†’ **Non-Constant Impossible (NN)**

**Informatics**:  
 â€¢ Stable processes and services, user-level programs striving to **maintain balance and operability** â†’ **NV**  
 â€¢ Errors and crashes, progressing toward **breakdown and system exit** â†’ **NN**

---

# \[9\] The Necessity of Distinguishability and Its Properties {#[9]-the-necessity-of-distinguishability-and-its-properties}

ğŸ”¹ 1\. Brief Statement

In order to exist, one must be distinguishable. Everything that exists is distinct both from the impossible and from any other existing entity.

---

ğŸ”¹ 2\. Interpretation and Significance

**Distinguishability** is the foundation of the structure of Being and the fundamental criterion for the possibility of existence.  
 Without distinctions, there can be no objects, no concepts, no logic, and no consciousness.  
 The Model of Conscious Volitional Becoming (CVB) asserts: distinguishability is not an optional feature, but a **precondition of Being**.  
 A difference is not merely a variation of properties â€” it is the **ontological boundary** between â€œisâ€ and â€œis not.â€  
 Loss of distinguishability leads either to **chaos** (â‰ˆ everything at once) or to **emptiness** (â‰ˆ nothing at all).  
 Thus, distinguishability structures the Field of the Possible:  
 every entity must possess properties that distinguish it from others and from the impossible.

---

ğŸ”¹ 3\. Formulas

These formulas represent the basis for two sub-axioms:

#  **\[9.1\] Difference** {#[9.1]-difference}

 **Difference** â€” Difference as a relation that defines non-identity of properties

# **\[9.2\] Identity** {#[9.2]-identity}

 **Identity** â€” Identity as the impossibility of difference with oneself

Symbolic Form:  
Î”(x, y)                                  â€” x and y are distinguishable    
Â¬Î”(x, x)                                 â€” nothing is distinguishable from itself    
x â‰  y â‡’ âˆƒF (F(x) âˆ§ Â¬F(y))                â€” difference requires at least one differing predicate    
âˆ€x âˆ€y \[(âˆ€F (F(x) â‡” F(y))) â†’ x \= y\]       â€” only fully coinciding objects are identical    
Â¬âˆƒF: F(z) â‰  Â¬F(z) â‡’ z âˆ‰ W                â€” if an entity is not distinguishable by any predicate, it does not exist

LaTeX:  
\\Delta(x, y)    
\\quad \\neg \\Delta(x, x)    
\\quad x \\neq y \\Rightarrow \\exists F \\big(F(x) \\wedge \\neg F(y)\\big)    
\\quad \\forall x \\forall y \\big\[(\\forall F (F(x) \\leftrightarrow F(y))) \\rightarrow x \= y\\big\]    
\\quad \\neg \\exists F: F(z) \\neq \\neg F(z) \\Rightarrow z \\notin W

---

ğŸ”¹ 4\. Logical Justification

From \[4\]: Possible â‰  Impossible â†’ **clear distinction is required**  
 From \[1\]: Absolute Nothing contains no distinctions â†’ distinguishability is a **mark of the Possible**  
 From \[9\]: The structure of reality requires differentiation for **sustainable Becoming**

Therefore:

* **Anti-reflexivity** (Â¬Î”(x,x)) â€” nothing differs from itself

* **Completeness of distinction** (x â‰  y â‡’ âˆƒF) â€” two distinct entities must differ by at least one predicate

Sub-axioms **\[9.1\] Difference** and **\[9.2\] Identity** formalize the foundational relations of distinguishability and identity.  
 â†’ Distinguishability is necessary for: **existence, stability, logic, memory, and morality**

---

ğŸ”¹ 5\. Responses to Objections

**1\. Quantum Superposition:**  
 â€ƒâ€œStates can be indistinguishable.â€  
 â†’ **Response**: Superposition is not the negation of difference, but the **temporary coexistence** of possible forms **prior to the act of distinction** (i.e., measurement).

**2\. Non-identity logics (paraconsistency):**  
 â€ƒâ€œOne can build logics where mismatched definitions are allowed.â€  
 â†’ **Response**: These logics function within **restricted domains** and still require **strictly localized distinctions**, thereby confirming â€” not refuting â€” the necessity of distinguishability.

**3\. Absolute Unity (Monism):**  
 â€ƒâ€œAll is One; differences are illusions.â€  
 â†’ **Response**: Complete identity collapses logic and renders all assertion impossible.  
 Even the claim â€œall is oneâ€ presupposes a distinction between â€œunityâ€ and â€œnon-unity.â€

---

ğŸ”¹ 6\. Clarification of Terms

**\[9.1\] Difference** â€” the logical and ontological foundation for the distinction between entities.  
 â€ƒâ€ƒ**Î”(x, y)** â€” Difference between x and y: the presence of at least one distinguishing predicate.

**\[9.2\] Identity** â€” the impossibility of distinction between an entity and itself.  
 â€ƒâ€ƒ**Â¬Î”(x, x)** â€” Nothing can differ from itself; any such difference would indicate a different object.

âš  Note: the claim â€œnothing differs from itselfâ€ is valid only as an **instantaneous logical condition**.  
 **Identity** in this model â‰  absence of change.

In **non-static Becoming**, identity is preserved **not** through full property coincidence but through:  
 â€¢ **\[10.3\] Memory** â€” the bearer of distinguishability  
 â€¢ **\[10.3.5\] Name Space** â€” the system preserving the identity of changing forms

**W** â€” the set of all possible (distinguishable and stable) entities.

---

ğŸ”¹ 7\. Understanding for All (Popular Version)

In order for something to **exist**, it must be **different** from Nothing.  
 If nothing were different from anything else, everything would collapse into **a formless grey mush** â€” no thoughts, no feelings, no world.

**Distinction** is what makes things **real**:  
 You recognize a face **because it differs** from others.  
 You remember an event **because it stands out** from the rest.

---

ğŸ”¹ 8\. Empirical Examples

**Logic**:

* Law of Identity (A \= A), Law of Non-Contradiction (A â‰  Â¬A). Without these, thought is impossible.

**Mathematics**:

* Binary code works **only** because of the distinction between 0 and 1

* Sets are defined by differences in elements. No difference â†’ no numbers, no algebra.

**Physics**:

* Particles differ by mass, spin, charge. Without these â€” no chemistry, no interactions.

**Everyday Experience**:

* You recognize a face because it differs from others.

* You remember an event because it stands out from others.

---

# **\[III\] Structure** {#[iii]-structure}
